The Refutation of Mu'tazila on Lam al-Aqibah
Nasafi presents the Mu'tazilite claim and refutes it using logic and analogy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Mu'tazila's claim regarding lam al-aqibah and the Maturidi refutation based on Allah's omniscience.

Core Idea
Lam al-aqibah cannot apply to Allah because He is not ignorant of outcomes.

In this passage, Nasafi presents a key argument in the debate over divine will and human accountability. The Mu'tazila attempt to reinterpret two Qur'anic verses using the grammatical concept of lam al-aqibah (the lam of consequence) to avoid attributing purposes to Allah that appear to lead to evil. However, Nasafi refutes this by showing that such a linguistic usage implies ignorance of outcomes, which cannot be attributed to Allah. Let us examine the argument step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the Ahl al-Haqq's proof
Start by reading the verses (3:178 and 7:179) and how the People of Truth argue from them. Notice that the verses use 'lam' indicating purpose.
2
Understand the Mu'tazila's objection
The Mu'tazila claim the 'lam' is for consequence, not purpose. They give examples like Moses and common sayings. Grasp their reasoning.
3
Analyze Nasafi's refutation
Nasafi points out that lam al-aqibah only makes sense for an agent ignorant of outcomes. Since Allah knows all, it cannot apply. Follow his logical argument.
This is the core of the refutation.
4
Reflect on the farmer analogy
Nasafi uses the analogy of a farmer sowing seeds knowing they won't grow. This illustrates the absurdity of attributing lam al-aqibah to Allah. Think about its force.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأهل الحق يحتجون بقوله تعالى: ﴿ وَلَا يَحْسَبَنَّ الَّذِينَ كَفَرُوا أَنَّمَا نُمْلِي هُمْ خَيْرٌ لأَنْفُسِهِمْ إِنَّمَا نُمْلِي لَهُمْ لِيَزْدَادُوا إِثْمًا ﴾ دلت الآية أنه أراد منهم ازدياد الإثم حيث أملى لهم ليزدادوا إثما، وقال تعالى: ﴿ وَلَقَدْ ذَرَأْنَا لِجَهَنَّمَ كَثِيرًا مِّنَ الْجِنِّ وَالْإِنسِ ﴾ ومن ذرأه لجهنم أراد منه ما به يصير لجهنم إذ لو ذرأه لجهنم مع إرادة ما به يصير للجنة فقد أراد فيه ما يصير بإدخاله ما ذرأه له ظالمًا، وهذا محال. ثم وزعمت المعتزلة أن اللام في الآيتين جميعًا لام العاقبة لا لام التعليل كما في قوله تعالى: ﴿ فَالْتَقَطَهُ آلُ فِرْعَوْنَ لِيَكُونَ لَهُمْ عَدُوًّا وَحَزَنًا ﴾ وهم ما التقطوه لهذا وإنما التقطوه ليكون لهم ولدًا وقرة عين، ولكن لما كان عاقبة أمره أن صار لهم عدوا ذكر هذه اللفظة وكما يقال: ولدوا للموت وبنوا للخراب، وأحد لا يلد للموت بل يطلب بقاء الولد ولا يبني للخراب ولكن للانتفاع بها، ولكن لما كان عاقبة أمر الولد الموت وعاقبة أمر الدار الخراب يقال: هذا لبيان العاقبة. والجواب إنما يتصور أن يريد أحد من الآخر ما لا يكون منه، ويفعل فعلاً له ولا يكون هو بل يكون غيره أو ضده، إن كان الفاعل جاهلاً بالعواقب فيفعل فعلاً لغرض فلا يحصل ذلك بل يحصل غيره، فأما من لا يجهل العواقب كيف يريد عاقبة لفعل يعلم حقيقة أنها لا تكون على ما يريد؟ وهل يفعل هذا إلا سفيه؟ ومثله في الشاهد كمن يبذر بذرا في الأرض ويريد خروج الزرع وحصول النماء، علمه أنه لا ينبت ولا يخرج، وكذا استعمال لام العاقبة فمن يجوز عليه الجهل بالعواقب فيفعل فعلاً لقصد فيحصل له ضد تلك العاقبة، ولا يحصل له ما هو المقصود، فيقال على طريق تعريف عاقبة فعله الوخيمة الحاصلة لا على وفق قصده ليتنبه لذلك فلا يعود إلى العمل بمثله فيما يستأنف من عمره، فأما في حق من هو علام الغيوب فاستعماله فاسد والله الموفق.
And the people of truth argue with His statement, exalted: 'And let not those who disbelieve think that Our prolonging [their life] is good for themselves. We only prolong [it] for them so that they may increase in sin.' The verse indicates that He desired from them increase of sin when He gave them respite so that they would increase in sin. And He said, exalted: 'And We have certainly created for Hell many of the jinn and mankind.' And whom He created for Hell, He desired from him that by which he becomes for Hell, for if He created him for Hell while desiring that by which he becomes for Paradise, then He would have desired for him that by which he enters what He created him for unjustly, and this is impossible. Then the Mu'tazila claimed that the 'lam' in both verses is the 'lam of consequence' not the 'lam of purpose', as in His statement, exalted: 'Then the family of Pharaoh picked him up to be for them an enemy and a cause of grief.' They did not pick him up for this; rather they picked him up so that he would be for them a son and a comfort, but since the consequence of his affair was that he became an enemy to them, they mentioned this wording. And just as it is said: they give birth for death and build for ruin, and no one gives birth for death but rather desires the survival of the child, and does not build for ruin but for benefit, but since the consequence of the child's affair is death and the consequence of the house's affair is ruin, it is said: this is to indicate the consequence. And the answer: It can only be conceived that one wills from another what will not be from him, and does an act for him and it does not occur but rather something else or its opposite occurs, if the agent is ignorant of consequences, so he does an act for a purpose but that purpose is not achieved rather something else is achieved. As for one who is not ignorant of consequences, how can he will a consequence for an act while he knows in truth that it will not be as he wills? And does anyone do this except a fool? And its likeness in the witnessed is like one who sows seeds in the ground and desires the emergence of crops and growth, while he knows that it will not sprout nor come out. Similarly, the use of the 'lam of consequence' is only for one who is subject to ignorance of consequences, so he does an act for a purpose and then the opposite of that consequence occurs for him, and what was intended does not occur for him, so it is said by way of informing of the evil consequence of his act that befell not in accordance with his purpose, so that he may be warned and not return to doing the like of it in what remains of his life. As for in the case of Him who is the Knower of the unseen, its use is invalid, and Allah is the giver of success.
Source pages p. 960

Commentary
This passage is a complete argumentation (proof, objection, and refutation) concerning the interpretation of certain Quranic verses. It begins by presenting the proof of Ahl al-Haqq (the People of Truth) from two verses: 3:178 and 7:179. From the first verse, they deduce that Allah desired the increase of sin for the disbelievers by giving them respite. From the second verse, they argue that since Allah created many jinn and mankind for Hell, He must have desired from them that which leads them to Hell; otherwise, it would be unjust. Then the Mu'tazila raise an objection: they claim that the 'lam' in both verses is 'lam al-aqibah' (lam of consequence) indicating the eventual outcome, not 'lam al-ta'lil' (lam of purpose) indicating the intended purpose. They support this with the example of Pharaoh's family picking up Moses, where the apparent purpose was adoption but the consequence was enmity. They also use common sayings like 'they give birth for death' to show that such expressions denote consequence, not intention. The author then gives the answer: such use of 'lam al-aqibah' is only plausible for an agent ignorant of outcomes. A person may do an act with a certain purpose but arrive at a different consequence, prompting observers to describe the consequence. However, Allah is the Knower of the unseen and knows all outcomes exactly. It would be foolish for Him to will a consequence that He knows will not occur. Therefore, applying 'lam al-aqibah' to Allah's actions is invalid. The argument proceeds in a logical, step-by-step manner, using a clear analogy of a farmer sowing seeds knowing they will not grow.

Key Terms
لام العاقبة
لام التعليل
الجاهل بالعواقب
علام الغيوب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The lam in verses like 'liyazdādū ithman' can be interpreted as lam al-aqibah (consequence) rather than purpose.
Correction: Lam al-aqibah implies the agent is ignorant of the outcome, which cannot be said of Allah who is All-Knowing.

Checkpoint
Why does Nasafi reject the Mu'tazilite use of 'lam al-aqibah' in reference to Allah's actions?
A) Because Allah is not described by purpose or will.
B) Because 'lam al-aqibah' can only apply to an agent who is ignorant of the consequences, which does not apply to Allah.
C) Because the verses in question do not contain the particle 'lam'.
D) Because the Mu'tazila misinterpreted the grammar of the verses.

Key Takeaway
The use of lam al-aqibah for Allah is invalid because it implies ignorance of consequences, whereas Allah is All-Knowing.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When have you acted as if Allah's plans might fail, doubting that He knows the outcome? How does this lesson convict you to trust His purpose even in uncertainty?
?
The lesson compares one who acts without knowledge of consequences to a fool. Examine your own decisions: are there areas where you proceed without seeking Allah's guidance, assuming you know the outcome? How will you change that today?
?
Allah's actions have a purpose, even when the consequence appears negative. Where in your life do you need to repent of complaining about outcomes, recognizing that Allah's purpose is greater than your understanding?

Proof from Quran 6:125: Guidance and Misguidance Are from Allah's Will
Nasafi cites Quran 6:125 as direct proof that guidance and misguidance are from Allah's will.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Nasafi uses Quran 6:125 as a direct scriptural proof that both guidance and misguidance are caused solely by Allah's will, refuting the Mu'tazilite position of human autonomy.

Core Idea
Allah's will directly determines both guidance and misguidance.

Having just refuted the Mu'tazilite claim that humans create their own acts, Nasafi now anchors the Maturidi position in a clear Quranic verse. This verse directly links the expansion or constriction of the heart to Allah's will, making divine predestination explicit. Pay close attention to how the author draws his conclusion from the verse.

Guided Path
1
Read the verse carefully
Read the Arabic of Quran 6:125 and its translation. Notice that the verse presents two opposite conditions: Allah 'wants to guide' and 'wants to misguide', each with a corresponding outcome in the breast.
The verse is self-contained and foundational to the discussion of qadar.
2
Identify the author's conclusion
After the verse, Nasafi makes an explicit inference. Find the sentence beginning with 'فجعل' (So He made) and understand which part of the verse he highlights.
The conclusion connects the verse directly to the doctrine of divine predestination.
3
Reflect on the theological implication
Ask yourself: If Allah makes the expansion of the breast the means by which faith is attained, can a person attain faith without Allah's will? How does this verse refute the idea that humans create their own faith?
This verse is a cornerstone for the Maturidi argument on qadar.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقال تعالى: ﴿ فَمَن يُرِدِ اللهُ أَن يَهْدِيَهُ يَشْرَحْ صَدْرَهُ لِلْإِسْلَامِ وَمَن يُرِدْ أَن يُضِلَهُ يَجْعَلْ صَدْرَهُ ضَيِّقًا حَرَبًا ﴾ فجعل شرح الصدر سببًا يحصل به الإيمان، وضيق الصدر
And He said, exalted: 'So whoever Allah wants to guide, He expands his breast for Islam; and whoever He wants to misguide, He makes his breast tight and constricted.' So He made the expansion of the breast a means by which faith is attained, and the constriction of the breast
Source pages p. 961

Commentary
This passage is a proof text from the Quran immediately following the previous refutation. It directly quotes verse 6:125, which states that Allah expands the breast for Islam for whom He wills to guide, and makes the breast tight and constricted for whom He wills to misguide. The author then draws a conclusion: Allah made the expansion of the breast a means (sabab) by which faith (iman) is attained. This establishes that both guidance and misguidance are directly caused by Allah's will, countering the Mu'tazilite position that humans create their own acts. The verse also implies that the 'constriction of the breast' is the means leading to disbelief, though the sentence is cut off. This is a concise proof grounding the doctrine of divine predestination in a clear, self-evident scriptural statement.

Key Terms
إرادة الله
الهداية
الضلال
شرح الصدر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that 'whoever Allah wants to guide' means Allah merely sets up conditions without actively determining the outcome, or that the verse only applies to believers and not to the process of becoming a believer.
Correction: Nasafi's conclusion demonstrates that Allah's 'wanting to guide' directly causes the expansion of the breast, which is the means by which faith is attained. This shows active determination, not just passive condition-setting. The verse is universal in its application to all people, not limited to believers.

Checkpoint
What does Nasafi conclude from Quran 6:125 about the relationship between Allah's will and faith?
A) Allah only guides those who first choose faith themselves.
B) Allah makes the expansion of the breast the means by which faith is attained, linking guidance directly to His will.
C) The verse only refers to the afterlife, not this world.
D) The constriction of the breast is purely metaphorical and not a real cause.

Key Takeaway
Quran 6:125 directly proves that guidance and misguidance are caused by Allah's will, as the expansion or constriction of the breast is the divinely created means for attaining faith or disbelief.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you feel your heart open to faith and good deeds, do you acknowledge that Allah, by His will, expanded your chest? What specific dua will you make tomorrow morning to ask Him to keep your heart wide open for Islam?
?
If misguidance is directly from Allah's will, does that thought make you tremble before Him? What will you change in your daily routine to humble yourself and seek His protection from a sealed heart?
?
Think of a time you felt spiritually constricted. Did you immediately recognize it as a sign from Allah calling you back to Him? Tonight, will you repent sincerely and ask Him to replace that tightness with expansion?

Why Lam al-'Aqibah Cannot Apply to Allah
Al-Nasafi refutes the claim that Allah uses lam al-'aqibah like humans.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why lam al-'aqibah cannot be applied to Allah because it presupposes ignorance of consequences.

Core Idea
Lam al-'aqibah presupposes ignorance, so it cannot apply to the All-Knower.

This passage from Imam al-Nasafi refutes a claim about the Arabic linguistic expression lam al-'aqibah. Some argued that certain Qur'anic phrases use this lām to indicate an outcome contrary to intention, and thus it could apply to Allah. Al-Nasafi shows that this usage only makes sense for one who is ignorant of consequences, which is impossible for Allah. Through a logical argument and a vivid analogy, he demonstrates the absurdity of attributing such a linguistic device to the All-Knowing.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the literal translation. Notice the author's style of presenting a claim and then refuting it.
The passage uses a specific term 'lam al-'aqibah' which is a type of lām in Arabic grammar.
2
Identify the opposing claim and the refutation
Find where al-Nasafi quotes the opponent's claim about the outcomes of a child's affair and a house's ruin. Then locate his answer and the condition he sets for lam al-'aqibah to be valid.
The key condition is that the agent must be ignorant of consequences (جاهلاً بالعواقب).
3
Understand the analogy and its implication
Study the analogy of the farmer who sows seeds knowing they won't grow. Ask yourself: Why would such an action be foolish? Then relate it back to the main point: Allah cannot be described as using lam al-'aqibah.
The conclusion is clear: 'As for the case of the All-Knower of the Unseen, its use is invalid.'

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الرد على زعمهم
عاقبة أمر الولد الموت وعاقبة أمر الدار الخراب يقال : هذا لبيان العاقبة (١).
والجواب إنما يتصور أن يريد أحد من الآخر ما لا يكون منه، ويفعل فعلاً له ولا (٢) يكون هو بل يكون غيره أو ضده ، إن كان الفاعل جاهلاً بالعواقب فيفعل فعلاً لغرض فلا يحصل ذلك بل يحصل غيره، فأما من لا يجهل العواقب كيف يريد عاقبة لفعل يعلم حقيقة أنها لا تكون على ما يريد؟ وهل يفعل هذا إلا سفيه؟ ومثله في الشاهد كمن يبذر بذرا في الأرض ويريد خروج الزرع وحصول النماء، علمه أنه لا ينبت ولا يخرج، وكذا استعمال لام العاقبة فمن يجوز عليه الجهل بالعواقب فيفعل فعلاً لقصد فيحصل له ضد (۳) تلك العاقبة، ولا يحصل له ما هو المقصود، فيقال على طريق تعريف عاقبة فعله الوخيمة الحاصلة لا على وفق قصده ليتنبه لذلك فلا يعود إلى العمل بمثله فيما يستأنف من عمره، فأما (٤) في حق من هو علام الغيوب فاستعماله فاسد والله الموفق.
The refutation of their claim: The outcome of a child's affair is death, and the outcome of a house's affair is ruin. It is said: 'This is for stating the consequence (lam al-'aqibah).' The answer: It is only conceivable that one intends from another what is not from him, and does an action for him while it is not (the intended outcome) but rather something else or its opposite, if the agent is ignorant of consequences; then he does an action for a purpose, but that purpose does not occur, rather something else occurs. As for one who is not ignorant of consequences, how can he intend a consequence for an action while he knows in truth that it will not be as he intends? Does anyone do this except a fool? Its parallel in observable reality is like one who sows a seed in the ground and wants the plant to come out and growth to occur, while he knows that it will not grow or come out. Likewise, the use of lam al-'aqibah is only when one is susceptible to ignorance of consequences, so he does an action for a purpose, but the opposite of that consequence occurs for him, and what was intended does not occur; then it is said by way of informing him of the dire consequence that actually occurs, not in accordance with his intention, so that he may be warned and not return to similar action in what remains of his life. As for the case of the All-Knower of the Unseen ('Allam al-Ghuyub), its use is invalid. And Allah grants success.
Source pages p. 961

Commentary
This passage refutes the claim that the Qur'anic expression 'lam al-'aqibah' (the lām of consequence) can be applied to Allah's actions. The author begins by stating the opposing view: that phrases like 'the outcome of a child is death' exemplify lam al-'aqibah, i.e., a lām indicating that something ends up being the case, regardless of intention. The response then argues that such usage only makes sense when the agent is ignorant of the true outcome. A person may do something intending X, but Y occurs instead due to ignorance. But for one who knows all consequences with certainty, it is impossible to intend an outcome that he knows will not happen; that would be foolish. The author gives the analogy of a farmer who sows seeds knowing they will not grow—he would not expect a harvest. Therefore, lam al-'aqibah applies only where ignorance is possible. Since Allah is 'Allam al-Ghuyub (the All-Knower of the Unseen), He cannot be described as using lam al-'aqibah, as it would imply foolishness. The passage concludes that such usage regarding Allah is invalid.

Key Terms
لام العاقبة (lam al-'aqibah)
جاهل بالعواقب (ignorant of consequences)
علام الغيوب (All-Knower of the Unseen)
سفيه (foolish one)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The use of lam al-'aqibah in the Qur'an shows that Allah can intend an outcome different from what actually happens.
Correction: Lam al-'aqibah is only used when the agent is ignorant of the true outcome; since Allah is all-knowing, it cannot apply to Him.

Checkpoint
According to the author, what condition must be present for the use of lam al-'aqibah to be valid?
A) The agent must be all-knowing.
B) The agent must be unaware of the actual result.
C) The agent must intend the opposite of what happens.
D) The agent must be a human being.

Key Takeaway
Lam al-'aqibah is incompatible with divine omniscience because it only applies when ignorance is present, and Allah is free from all ignorance.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you act, do you ever assume you know the outcome, only to be surprised? How does this remind you that your knowledge is limited, and that only Allah truly knows the end of every affair? What one area of your life do you need to surrender to His knowledge today?
?
The farmer in the analogy sows seeds knowing they will not grow. Are there habits, relationships, or pursuits in your life that you persist in despite knowing they bear no good fruit? What would it take for you to stop sowing where only ruin will grow?
?
If you truly believed that Allah sees every hidden consequence and that His knowledge is perfect, would you make different choices in secret? What is one thing you do in private that you would never do if you fully internalized that Allah is 'Allam al-Ghuyub?

Refuting the Mu'tazilite Tawil of God's Will to Misguide
Refuting the Mu'tazilite tawil of the verse on God's will to misguide.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Mu'tazilite interpretation of God's will to misguide in Quran 11:34 is invalid according to Imam al-Nasafi.

Core Idea
If God cannot will misguidance, Noah's statement would affirm the opposite.

Imam al-Nasafi turns to a key verse used by the Mu'tazilites to deny that God wills misguidance. He presents their interpretation and then dismantles it with a logical argument: if the condition 'if God desires to misguide you' is impossible, then the negation of benefit becomes an affirmation. But the context shows Noah spoke out of despair, confirming that God did will their misguidance. This lesson traces his refutation step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the verse citation and the author's logical turn.
2
Identify the Mu'tazilite claim
The author states the Mu'tazilite interpretation: the verse only says advice does not benefit if God wills misguidance, not that He actually wills it. Find this in the text.
3
Understand the logical refutation
The author argues that if willing misguidance is impossible, then suspending the negation of benefit on that impossible condition actually affirms the benefit. Trace this logical move.
This is the core of the refutation.
4
See how Noah's context confirms the refutation
Noah spoke out of despair, meaning he knew God did will their misguidance. The author uses this to show the Mu'tazilite interpretation fails.
Context is key.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ضالاً صادقا أم كاذبًا؟ فإن قالوا: كان صادقًا ظهرت مكابرتهم، وإن قالوا: كان كاذبًا، قيل : كان إذا مريدًا كونه كاذبًا في تسميته ضالاً وهو سفه – جل الله تعالى عن ذلك. وقال تعالى خبرًا عن نوح عليه السلام حيث قال لقومه: ﴿ وَلَا يَنفَعُكُمْ نُصْحِيَ إِنْ أَرَدتُ أَنْ أَنصَحَ لَكُمْ إِن كَانَ اللهُ يُرِيدُ أَن يُغْوِيَكُمْ ﴾ ذكر أن الله يريد أن يغوي الكفرة، وتأويل المعتزلة أن في الآية أن نصحة لا ينفع إن كان الله يريد أن يغويهم وليس فيه أنه يريد، تأويل فاسد ، لأنه إذا كان يستحيل منه إرادة غوايتهم أي فائدة في ذكر الآية على الأمر، لو كان كما يزعمون لكان ينبغي أن يكون مراد نوح عليه السلام من هذه الآية بيان أن نصحه ينفعهم لا محالة، لأن فيه تعليق نفي نفع النصح بما يستحيل ثبوته وهو إرادة إغوائهم، وتعليق النفي بما يستحيل ثبوته يكون تأكيدًا للإثبات، ويصير كأنه قال : لا ينفعكم نصحي، إذا كان الله يريد أن يغويكم فإذا استحال أن يريد أن يغويكم ينفعكم نصحي وحيث رأينا أنه كان لا ينفعهم وإنما قال ذلك يأسا من نفع نصحه لهم عند إرادة الله أن يغويهم، فكان ذلك دليلاً على فساد التأويل.
Misguided, truthful or lying? If they say: he was truthful, their stubbornness appears, and if they say: he was lying, it is said: then he intended to be lying in calling him misguided and that is foolish – Exalted is God above that. And God Most High said, reporting from Noah, peace be upon him, when he said to his people: 'And my advice will not benefit you if I intend to advise you, if God desires to misguide you.' He mentioned that God desires to misguide the disbelievers. The Mu'tazilites' interpretation is that in the verse, his advice does not benefit if God desires to misguide them, and it does not contain that He desires it. An invalid interpretation, because if it is impossible for Him to will their misguidance, what benefit is there in mentioning the verse in this matter? If it were as they claim, it would be necessary that the intended meaning of Noah, peace be upon him, in this verse be a statement that his advice benefits them inevitably, because in it the negation of the benefit of advice is suspended by something whose establishment is impossible, namely the willing of their misguidance. And suspending negation by what is impossible to establish is an affirmation of the positive, and it becomes as if he said: My advice does not benefit you if God wills to misguide you. So if it is impossible that He wills to misguide you, my advice benefits you. And since we saw that it did not benefit them and he said that out of despair of the benefit of his advice to them when God willed to misguide them, that was evidence of the invalidity of the interpretation.
Source pages p. 964

Commentary
This passage refutes the Mu'tazilite interpretation of Quranic verse 11:34. The author begins by presenting a previous argument about calling someone misguided (ضالاً) – possibly in another context – but then focuses on the verse. The Mu'tazilites claim that the verse 'If God desires to misguide you' does not actually affirm that God desires misguidance; they interpret it as a hypothetical condition. The author argues that if it is impossible for God to will misguidance, then Noah's statement becomes meaningless. If the condition is impossible, then the apodosis (no benefit) would be a rhetorical affirmation that advice benefits. But Noah clearly said it out of despair, indicating that God did will their misguidance. Thus the Mu'tazilite tawil is invalid.

Key Terms
الضال
إرادة الإغواء
تأويل المعتزلة
تعليق النفي بما يستحيل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the Mu'tazilite interpretation is plausible because it avoids attributing evil to God.
Correction: The author shows that this interpretation contradicts the clear meaning of the verse and the context of Noah's despair.

Checkpoint
Why does the author consider the Mu'tazilite interpretation of the verse invalid?
A) Because the Mu'tazilites reject the authenticity of the verse.
B) Because suspending negation on an impossible condition would make the statement affirm the opposite, which contradicts Noah's despair.
C) Because the Mu'tazilites do not believe in divine will at all.
D) Because the verse is abrogated.

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazilite interpretation of Quran 11:34 is invalid because suspending a negation on an impossible condition would affirm the opposite, contradicting Noah's despair and the plain meaning of the verse.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read the verse 'If God desires to misguide you' (11:34), does it make you uncomfortable to think that God may will misguidance? Examine your heart: is there a part of you that wants to protect God from what you perceive as injustice, rather than submitting to His absolute sovereignty? Will you repent from that subtle form of elevating your own reason above revelation?
?
Noah spoke these words out of despair after centuries of calling his people. Have you ever felt that your efforts to guide someone were futile? Did you truly resign yourself to God's will, or did you secretly harbor resentment or disappointment? This lesson teaches that God's will prevails – even in misguidance. Can you accept that God may not guide whom you love, and still love Him completely?
?
The Mu'tazilites twisted the verse to avoid attributing misguidance to God, but the author exposed the logical contradiction. Are there any beliefs you hold about God that, upon honest inspection, are actually attempts to make God fit your sense of fairness rather than accepting what He has revealed about Himself? What would it cost you to surrender those ideas?

Refuting Jafar ibn Harb: When Consequences Prove Falsity
Refuting Jafar ibn Harb's claim about the verse.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why an argument that merely points out the consequences of an opponent's belief is insufficient unless the opponent acknowledges those consequences as corrupt.

Core Idea
Sound premises cannot yield corrupt consequences.

In this passage, Imam al-Nasafi refutes a particular interpretation of a Quranic verse. Jafar ibn Harb claimed that Noah's words were meant to rebuke a group of fatalists (jabariyya) who believed God wills corruption. Al-Nasafi argues that even if Noah's statement were intended to show the absurdity of their belief by pointing out its consequences, that would not work because the fatalists themselves did not see those consequences as absurd. This leads to a key dialectical principle: a conclusion's absurdity only refutes a premise if the opponent concedes the absurdity.

Guided Path
1
Introduce the debate
Read the first part of the passage where al-Nasafi states Jafar ibn Harb's claim and then rejects it. Notice how the claim is presented as an interpretation of the verse.
Jafar ibn Harb was a Mu'tazili theologian.
2
Understand the critique
Al-Nasafi argues that the interpretation is useless because it would not actually convince the jabariyya. He asks: what warning would occur? Find this rhetorical question in the text.
The jabariyya believed God creates all actions, including disbelief.
3
Grasp the logical principle
The author explains that denouncing a view by its consequences only works if the opponent admits those consequences are bad. The key line: 'الصحيح لا ينتج الفاسد' (the sound does not produce the corrupt). Understand this principle.
This is a standard logical principle in kalam.
4
Apply to the case
Since the jabariyya did not see the consequence (ineffectiveness of prophethood) as corrupt, the argument fails. Al-Nasafi concludes that Jafar's interpretation is a product of confusion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وما قاله جعفر بن حرب أن الآية تدل أنه كان في قوم نوح عليه السلام قوم مجبرة يقولون : إن الله تعالى يريد الفساد فخاطبهم منبها لهم على بطلان قولهم فقال: وَلَا يَنفَعُكُمْ نُصْحِي إِنْ أَرَدتُ أَنْ أَنصَحَ لَكُمْ فيما أدعوكم إن كان الأمر كما ذكرتم من أنه تعالى المريد لفسادكم ويخلق الكفر فيكم. فاسد، لأن الأمر لو كان كما زعم جعفر بن حرب أي تنبيه يحصل لأولئك بهذا القول؟ وأي إلزام حجة بذلك؟ وأكثر ما في الباب أنك تقول - يشنع عليهم بذلك: إن على مقالتكم هذه لا ينفع بعث الأنبياء مبشرين ومنذرين ولا الدعاء إلى الله تعالى، وأن أولئك كانوا منكرين بعث الأنبياء والدعاء على ألسنتهم إلى الله تعالى وتشنيع مقالة بما يفضي إليه المقالة، وأهل المقالة يعتقدون صحته لا يجدي نفعا إنما ينفع ذلك أن لو كانت المقالة تفضي إلى أمر يعترف صاحب المقالة بفساده ويقر ببطلانه فيستدل عليه فيقال: لو كانت مقالتك حقًا لما أفضت إلى هذا الفاسد، إذ الصحيح لا ينتج الفاسد، وإنما الفاسد هو الذي ينتج الفاسد، فأما إذا كان صاحب المقالة لا يقر بفساد ما أفضت إليه مقالته لم يكن للاحتجاج بذلك عليه منفعة ولا فيه حكمة، فدل أن هذا فاسد دفعته إليه الحيرة.
And what Jafar ibn Harb said, that the verse indicates that among the people of Noah, peace be upon him, there were a people of jabariyya who say: God Most High wills corruption, so he addressed them to alert them to the falsity of their statement, saying: 'And my advice will not benefit you if I intend to advise you' in what I call you to, if the matter is as you have mentioned, that He is the One who wills your corruption and creates disbelief in you. [This is] invalid, because if the matter were as Jafar ibn Harb claimed, what warning would occur for those people by this statement? And what compelling argument is there in that? The most that can be said is that you say – to denounce them by it: Indeed, according to your statement, sending prophets as bringers of good news and warners does not benefit, nor does calling to God Most High. And those people were deniers of sending prophets and of calling with their tongues to God Most High. Denouncing a statement by what the statement leads to, while the proponents of the statement believe in its validity, is of no benefit. It only benefits if the statement leads to something that the proponent concedes is corrupt and acknowledges its falsity, so that one can argue against him: If your statement were true, it would not lead to this corrupt consequence, because sound does not produce corrupt, and only corrupt produces corrupt. But if the proponent does not concede the corruption of what his statement leads to, there is no benefit in arguing against him with it, nor is there wisdom in it. So it indicates that this is corrupt, driven by confusion.
Source pages p. 964

Commentary
This passage refutes Jafar ibn Harb's interpretation of the verse. Jafar claimed that Noah was addressing a group of jabariyya (fatalists) who believed God wills corruption. The author argues that such an interpretation is useless because even if Noah's statement were designed to show the absurdity of their belief by pointing out that it negates the benefit of prophecy, the jabariyya themselves would not accept that premise. For an argument to be effective, the opponent must acknowledge the absurdity of the consequence. Since the jabariyya believed in their own position, they would not see the consequence as absurd. Thus Jafar's interpretation is a product of confusion.

Key Terms
جعفر بن حرب
المجبرة
الاحتجاج
تشنيع المقالة
الصحيح لا ينتج الفاسد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that pointing out the consequences of an opponent's view is always sufficient refutation.
Correction: The author shows it only works if the opponent already concedes the badness of those consequences.

Checkpoint
Why does the author reject Jafar ibn Harb's interpretation?
A) Because Jafar ibn Harb is not a reliable narrator.
B) Because the argument from consequences only works if the opponent acknowledges the badness of the consequence.
C) Because the verse actually proves the jabariyya were correct.
D) Because Noah was not addressing jabariyya.

Key Takeaway
The author demonstrates that an argument from consequences only refutes an opponent if the opponent admits the consequence is corrupt.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hold a strong opinion about religion, do you ever honestly trace its logical consequences to see where they lead, even if the result is uncomfortable? Or do you, like the jabariyya, simply deny the consequence is bad?
?
Think of a belief you hold that some might consider corrupt. Would you be willing to admit the corruption if you were shown that the belief leads to an absurd conclusion? Or would you resist, protecting your pride over truth?
?
Al-Nasafi says a refutation only works if the opponent concedes the consequence is corrupt. In your own life, are there beliefs you defend without honestly evaluating their outcomes? How can you cultivate the courage to say 'if this leads to that, I must be wrong'?

Refuting al-Jubba'i on Divine Will and Misguidance
Refuting al-Jubba'i's interpretation of 'yurid an yughwiyakum' as deprivation of reward.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why al-Jubba'i's interpretation of 'yurid an yughwiyakum' as deprivation of reward is invalid, based on both linguistic evidence and the theological dilemma it creates.

Core Idea
Interpreting 'misguidance' as 'deprivation' leads to linguistic and theological absurdity.

This passage tackles a Mu'tazilite attempt to reinterpret a Qur'anic verse that seems to attribute the desire for misguidance to Allah. Al-Jubba'i argued that it means deprivation of reward, but the author shows this fails both linguistically and rationally. We'll follow the refutation step by step.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Mu'tazilite background
Briefly recall that Mu'tazilites like al-Jubba'i deny that Allah wills evil or misguidance. They try to reinterpret verses that imply otherwise. Here, al-Jubba'i claims 'yurid an yughwiyakum' means 'He deprives you of reward'.
2
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage carefully, then the literal translation. Notice the structure: first a linguistic objection, then a dilemma presented as a question with two possible answers.
The passage ends abruptly, but the argument is complete as given.
3
Analyze the linguistic refutation
The author first rejects al-Jubba'i's interpretation on lexical grounds: the Arabic language does not use 'ighwa' to mean deprivation. This is a simple but powerful argument.
Linguistic precision is key in kalam.
4
Examine the theological dilemma
The author then poses a dilemma: Does Allah will deprivation while also willing faith, or while also willing disbelief? The first option implies injustice (rewarding faith with deprivation), the second contradicts Mu'tazilite doctrine. Either way, al-Jubba'i's position is untenable.
Follow the two horns of the dilemma closely.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وما ذكره الجبائي أن معنى قوله: ﴿ يُرِيدُ أَن يُغْوِيَكُمْ ﴾ أي يحرمكم الثواب فاسد، لأن أهل اللغة لم يعرفوا الإغواء عبارة عن الحرمان والخيبة، على أنا نقول: الله تعالى على زعمكم - يريد حرمانهم عن الثواب وخيبتهم عن وهو لا يريد كفرهم أو يريد ذلك وهو يريد إيمانهم؟ فإن قال: يريد ذلك وهو يريد إيمانهم فقد أخبر أنه يرد الجور على زعمهم لأنه لو تحقق ما يريد بأن وجد منهم الإيمان وحرمهم عن الثواب وخيبهم عنه كان ذلك عنده ظلمًا، فإنه أراد ذلك فقد أراد ما هو ظلم، وهو يأبى أن يريد الله تعالى ما هو ظلم من غيره لقبح الظلم، فزعم أنه يريد الظلم من نفسه أنه قبيح، وهذه جهالة فاحشة. وإن قال: يريد ذلك وهو يريد كفرهم ترك مذهبه وانقاد للحق، وكذا تأويل
And what al-Jubba'i mentioned, that the meaning of His saying: 'He desires to misguide you' is that He deprives you of reward, is invalid, because the people of language do not know 'ighwa' (misguidance) as an expression for deprivation and disappointment. Moreover, we say: God Most High, according to your claim, desires to deprive them of reward and disappoint them, while He does not desire their disbelief – or He desires that while He desires their faith? If he says: He desires that while He desires their faith, then he has informed that He does injustice according to their claim, because if what He desires is realized – that faith occurs from them and He deprives them of reward and disappoints them – that would be, in his view, oppression. Since He desired that, He desired what is oppression, and He is above willing what is oppression from others due to the ugliness of oppression. So he claimed that He desires oppression from Himself, which is ugly. This is extreme ignorance. And if he says: He desires that while He desires their disbelief, he leaves his school and submits to the truth. And likewise the interpretation...
Source pages p. 965

Commentary
This passage refutes al-Jubba'i's (a Mu'tazilite) interpretation of 'He desires to misguide you' as 'He deprives you of reward.' First, the author rejects it on linguistic grounds: 'ighwa' does not mean deprivation. Second, he presents a dilemma: either God desires deprivation while also desiring their faith (which would be unjust, as it would mean rewarding faith with deprivation, and God is not unjust), or God desires deprivation while also desiring their disbelief (which would mean God wills both, aligning with the Maturidi position). If al-Jubba'i chooses the first, he attributes injustice to God; if the second, he abandons his Mu'tazilite position. Thus his interpretation is invalid.

Key Terms
الجبائي
الإغواء
الحرمان
الخيبة
الظلم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that 'yurid an yughwiyakum' can be metaphorically interpreted as deprivation of reward.
Correction: The author shows that 'ighwa' does not linguistically mean deprivation, and even if it did, it leads to a theological dilemma that either attributes injustice to Allah or contradicts Mu'tazilite doctrine.

Checkpoint
According to the author, what is the problem with al-Jubba'i's interpretation that 'yurid an yughwiyakum' means 'He deprives them of reward'?
A) It contradicts the Arabic language.
B) It leads to either attributing injustice to God or abandoning Mu'tazilite doctrine.
C) The Quran explicitly prohibits such interpretation.
D) Both A and B.

Key Takeaway
Al-Jubba'i's interpretation fails because it either contradicts Arabic or forces an unjust characterization of Allah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read that al-Jubba'i's interpretation forces the conclusion that Allah would will oppression, does it shake your own confidence in any theological positions you hold that might have similar consequences? What would it take for you to abandon an interpretation upon seeing such a logical inconsistency?
?
If someone today argued that a difficult Quranic verse should be interpreted figuratively to avoid a challenging theological implication, how would you apply the author's method of first checking linguistic usage before accepting the metaphor? Are you willing to insist on the literal meaning even when it makes you uncomfortable?
?
The author uses a dilemma to force al-Jubba'i into a corner. Are there any areas in your own understanding of Allah's attributes where you might be holding two incompatible beliefs without realizing it? Will you prayerfully examine your heart for such contradictions and resolve them with the same rigorous logic?

The Linguistic Refutation of al-Jubba'i's Interpretation
Nasafi states al-Jubba'i's claim and gives a linguistic refutation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why al-Jubba'i's interpretation of 'ighwa' as deprivation of reward fails on linguistic grounds.

Core Idea
The Arabic language itself refutes al-Jubba'i's claim.

In this passage, Imam Nasafi begins his refutation of the Mu'tazili theologian al-Jubba'i by appealing to linguistics. Al-Jubba'i had reinterpreted the Quranic word 'ighwa' to mean 'deprivation of reward' to avoid attributing misguidance to God. Nasafi counters that this meaning has no basis in Arabic. Let's examine the argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation to grasp the core claim.
2
Identify the linguistic basis
Notice that Nasafi relies on the consensus of linguists ('ahl al-lugha') who do not recognize this meaning.
3
Appreciate the method
See how Nasafi uses a foundational discipline (linguistics) to critique a theological interpretation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وما ذكره الجبائي أن معنى قوله: ﴿ يُرِيدُ أَن يُغْوِيَكُمْ ﴾ أي يحرمكم الثواب فاسد، لأن أهل اللغة لم يعرفوا الإغواء عبارة عن الحرمان والخيبة، على أنا نقول: الله تعالى على زعمكم - يريد حرمانهم عن الثواب ذلك وخيبتهم عن [؟] وهو لا يريد كفرهم أو يريد ذلك وهو يريد إيمانهم؟ فإن قال: يريد ذلك وهو يريد إيمانهم فقد أخبر أنه يرد الجور على زعمهم لأنه لو تحقق ما يريد بأن وجد منهم الإيمان وحرمهم عن الثواب وخيبهم عنه كان ذلك عنده ظلمًا، فإنه أراد ذلك فقد أراد ما هو ظلم، وهو يأبى أن يريد الله تعالى ما هو ظلم من غيره لقبح الظلم، فزعم أنه يريد الظلم من نفسه أنه وهذه جهالة فاحشة مع قبيح. وإن قال: يريد ذلك وهو يريد كفرهم ترك مذهبه وانقاد للحق.
And what al-Jubba'i mentioned, that the meaning of His saying 'He intends to lead you astray' (yuridu an yughwiyakum) is that He deprives you of reward, is false. Because the linguists did not know 'ighwa' as an expression for deprivation and disappointment. Moreover, we say: Allah Almighty, according to your claim, intends to deprive them of that reward and disappoint them from [؟], while He does not intend their disbelief, or He intends that while He intends their faith? If he says: He intends that while He intends their faith, then he has stated that He intends injustice according to their claim, because if what He intended were realized, such that faith occurred from them and He deprived them of reward and disappointed them, that would be injustice in his view. For He intended that, and He intended what is injustice, and He refuses that Allah intends what is injustice from another due to the ugliness of injustice. So he claimed that He intends injustice from Himself? That is blatant ignorance with ugliness. And if he says: He intends that while He intends their disbelief, then he has abandoned his own school and submitted to the truth.
Source pages p. 965

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of al-Jubba'i's (a Mu'tazili) interpretation of the Quranic verse 'yuridu an yughwiyakum' (He intends to lead you astray). Al-Jubba'i claimed that 'ighwa' here means 'deprivation of reward'. The author gives two arguments against this. First, a linguistic argument: the Arabic language does not recognize 'ighwa' as meaning 'deprivation' or 'disappointment'. Second, a theological dilemma: if God intends to deprive people of reward while also intending their faith (as the Mu'tazila claim God wills faith for all), then that would mean God intends injustice, because rewarding faith with deprivation is unjust. But God is just and cannot intend injustice. Alternatively, if al-Jubba'i says God intends deprivation while also intending their disbelief, then he contradicts the Mu'tazili principle that God wills faith for believers. Thus, either way, al-Jubba'i's interpretation leads to an absurdity, showing it is false.

Key Terms
إغواء
حرمان الثواب
الجبائي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The word 'ighwa' can be reinterpreted to mean deprivation of reward.
Correction: Linguistically, 'ighwa' has no such meaning; it is not recognized by Arabic language authorities.

Checkpoint
According to Imam Nasafi, why is al-Jubba'i's interpretation of 'ighwa' false?
A) It contradicts the Quran.
B) It has no basis in the Arabic language.
C) It implies God is unjust.
D) It was rejected by all scholars.

Key Takeaway
Al-Jubba'i's interpretation fails because it does not conform to the established linguistic meaning of 'ighwa'.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever interpreted a verse of the Quran based on your own reasoning without first consulting the established Arabic meaning? How did that affect your understanding of Allah's words? Will you commit today to always verify your interpretations with reliable sources of language and tafsir?
?
This lesson shows that even a renowned scholar like al-Jubba'i can err by departing from linguistic reality. Are there areas of your faith where you rely on your own logic rather than the clear teachings of the Quran and Sunnah? What is one specific step you will take this week to bring your practice in line with established knowledge?
?
The refutation here hinges on the authority of the Arabic language. How seriously do you take learning Arabic to understand the Quran directly? If you have neglected it, what is the smallest, most concrete action you will take this week to begin or continue that journey?

The Theological Dilemma of al-Jubba'i's Interpretation
Nasafi presents a dilemma with two branches to refute al-Jubba'i.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Nasafi exposes a contradiction in al-Jubba'i's view by showing it leads to either attributing injustice to God or abandoning Mu'tazili doctrine.

Core Idea
Al-Jubba'i's interpretation either makes God unjust or destroys his own school.

Having refuted al-Jubba'i on linguistic grounds, Nasafi now presents a theological dilemma. He forces al-Jubba'i to choose between two options, both of which are problematic for the Mu'tazili position. This is a classic argument in Islamic theology (kalam) used to show the incoherence of a rival view.

Guided Path
1
Read the dilemma
Read the Arabic passage carefully. Note the two possibilities presented.
2
Analyze the first branch
If God intends deprivation while also intending faith, then He intends injustice, which is impossible for God.
3
Analyze the second branch
If God intends deprivation while also intending disbelief, then al-Jubba'i contradicts his own doctrine that God wills good for believers.
4
Understand the conclusion
Either way, al-Jubba'i's interpretation is refuted.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وما ذكره الجبائي أن معنى قوله: ﴿ يُرِيدُ أَن يُغْوِيَكُمْ ﴾ أي يحرمكم الثواب فاسد، لأن أهل اللغة لم يعرفوا الإغواء عبارة عن الحرمان والخيبة، على أنا نقول: الله تعالى على زعمكم - يريد حرمانهم عن الثواب ذلك وخيبتهم عن [؟] وهو لا يريد كفرهم أو يريد ذلك وهو يريد إيمانهم؟ فإن قال: يريد ذلك وهو يريد إيمانهم فقد أخبر أنه يرد الجور على زعمهم لأنه لو تحقق ما يريد بأن وجد منهم الإيمان وحرمهم عن الثواب وخيبهم عنه كان ذلك عنده ظلمًا، فإنه أراد ذلك فقد أراد ما هو ظلم، وهو يأبى أن يريد الله تعالى ما هو ظلم من غيره لقبح الظلم، فزعم أنه يريد الظلم من نفسه أنه وهذه جهالة فاحشة مع قبيح. وإن قال: يريد ذلك وهو يريد كفرهم ترك مذهبه وانقاد للحق.
And what al-Jubba'i mentioned, that the meaning of His saying 'He intends to lead you astray' (yuridu an yughwiyakum) is that He deprives you of reward, is false. Because the linguists did not know 'ighwa' as an expression for deprivation and disappointment. Moreover, we say: Allah Almighty, according to your claim, intends to deprive them of that reward and disappoint them from [؟], while He does not intend their disbelief, or He intends that while He intends their faith? If he says: He intends that while He intends their faith, then he has stated that He intends injustice according to their claim, because if what He intended were realized, such that faith occurred from them and He deprived them of reward and disappointed them, that would be injustice in his view. For He intended that, and He intended what is injustice, and He refuses that Allah intends what is injustice from another due to the ugliness of injustice. So he claimed that He intends injustice from Himself? That is blatant ignorance with ugliness. And if he says: He intends that while He intends their disbelief, then he has abandoned his own school and submitted to the truth.
Source pages p. 965

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of al-Jubba'i's (a Mu'tazili) interpretation of the Quranic verse 'yuridu an yughwiyakum' (He intends to lead you astray). Al-Jubba'i claimed that 'ighwa' here means 'deprivation of reward'. The author gives two arguments against this. First, a linguistic argument: the Arabic language does not recognize 'ighwa' as meaning 'deprivation' or 'disappointment'. Second, a theological dilemma: if God intends to deprive people of reward while also intending their faith (as the Mu'tazila claim God wills faith for all), then that would mean God intends injustice, because rewarding faith with deprivation is unjust. But God is just and cannot intend injustice. Alternatively, if al-Jubba'i says God intends deprivation while also intending their disbelief, then he contradicts the Mu'tazili principle that God wills faith for believers. Thus, either way, al-Jubba'i's interpretation leads to an absurdity, showing it is false.

Key Terms
حرمان الثواب
ظلم
إيمان
كفر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: It is possible for God to intend to deprive believers of reward without contradiction.
Correction: If God intends faith and also deprivation of reward, that would be unjust, contradicting God's justice.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if al-Jubba'i says God intends deprivation while also intending faith, what follows?
A) God's wisdom is confirmed.
B) God intends what is unjust.
C) Al-Jubba'i's interpretation is correct.
D) The verse is metaphorical.

Key Takeaway
By presenting a dilemma, Nasafi shows that al-Jubba'i's interpretation cannot be consistently maintained without either impugning God's justice or contradicting Mu'tazili doctrine.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Are there areas in your life where you try to reconcile your desires with God's justice by reinterpreting His attributes, knowing deep down that you are twisting the truth? What would it cost you to submit to the plain meaning of His commands?
?
If you were in al-Jubba'i's position, would you prefer to attribute an apparent injustice to God or to admit your own school of thought was wrong? Which is harder for you: letting go of a cherished belief or accepting that God's ways are beyond your complete understanding?
?
When you face a contradiction between what you want to believe about God and what the texts clearly state, do you have the courage to abandon your own reasoning and submit to the truth, even if it means upending your intellectual framework?

Refutation of Mu'tazili Interpretation of 'Yuridu an Yughwiyakum' and 'Fitna'
Nasafi refutes the Mu'tazili interpretation of 'ighwa' as punishment and criticizes 'Abd al-Jabbar.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Mu'tazili reinterpretation of 'ighwa' as punishment is logically flawed and why the Maturidi position is coherent.

Core Idea
Reinterpreting divine verses to avoid theological problems often creates new contradictions.

Imam Nasafi continues his critique of Mu'tazili hermeneutics by addressing their claim that 'yuridu an yughwiyakum' means 'He will punish you'. He shows that this interpretation leads to the same dilemma as before: does God intend to punish them while intending their disbelief or faith? He then criticizes 'Abd al-Jabbar for claiming such interpretations are clear, and proceeds to refute their understanding of 'fitna' in the Quran. This lesson will walk you through his argument and its refutation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation to get the flow of the argument.
Notice how Nasafi uses a dilemma structure.
2
Understand the dilemma for the 'punishment' interpretation
The same question applies: does God intend punishment while intending disbelief or faith? Either leads to a problem.
This mirrors the previous lesson.
3
Examine the critique of 'Abd al-Jabbar
Nasafi mocks the claim that these interpretations are 'clear', showing that if clear falsehood, it's fine, but if clear correctness, it's shameful.
This highlights the weakness of Mu'tazili tafsir.
4
Analyze the discussion of 'fitna'
The Mu'tazila interpret 'fitna' as obligation/test, but Nasafi shows this is wrong because the Prophet was not distressed by obligation.
The verse refers to punishment or trial.
5
Consider the overall lesson
Reflect on how Nasafi defends Maturidi theology by exposing the logical flaws in Mu'tazili reinterpretations.
This demonstrates the importance of sound tafsir methodology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكذا تأويل غيرهم أن المراد بقوله: ﴿ يُرِيدُ أَن يُغْوِيَكُمْ ﴾ أي يعاقبكم، وألغى يذكر ويراد به العذاب. قال الله تعالى: ﴿ فَسَوْفَ يَلْقَوْنَ غَيّا ﴾ أي عذابا. وجوابه كجواب تأويل الجبائي أنه يريد أن يعاقبهم وهو يريد منهم الكفر أو يريد أن يعاقبهم وهو يريد منهم الإيمان؟ فبأي الجوابين أجاب فالكلام على ما ذكرنا ذكر هذه الوجوه وحكى كل تأويل عن صاحبه عبد الجبار الرازي ثم قال: وكل هذا واضح. فإن أراد أنه واضح وجه بطلانه فهو كما أراد، وإن أراد أنه واضح وجه صحته فهو يقول بقول يجب به الاستحياء من الناس والاستغفار من الله تعالى، والتعجب من رجل يدعي الترأس على أهل نحلته والتبحر في علوم أصحابه. ثم يرضى بمثل هذه التأويلات مع وهائها وظهور فسادها لأول الفكرة، وما أصدق ما قيل: حبك الشيء يعمي ويصم. وقال الله تعالى: ﴿ وَمَن يُرِدِ اللهُ فِتْنَتَهُ فَلَن تَمْلِك لَهُ مِنَ اللَّهِ شَيْئًا ﴾ قيل: فتنته أي عذابه وقيل امتحانه بالرجم والقتل وإرادة ذلك بدون إرادة ما يستوجب به إرادة ظلم وتأويلهم أن قوله تعالى: فتنته أي تكليفه وامتحانه خطأ، لأن النبي عليه السلام ما كان يشق عليه ذلك، وما كان يسأل أن لا يكلف الله تعالى عباده وقال تعالى: ﴿ أُولَئِكَ الَّذِينَ لَمْ يُرِدِ اللهُ أَن يُطَهِّرَ قُلُوبَهُمْ ﴾ وعند المعتزلة أراد ذلك وفي الآيات كثرة، ولهم اعتراضات عليها فاسدة لا معنى للاشتغال بذلك لوقوف من له أدنى علم على بطلان تلك الاعتراضات.
And likewise the interpretation of others that the intended meaning of His saying 'He intends to lead you astray' is that He will punish you, and they ignored that it is mentioned and intended as punishment. Allah Almighty said: 'Then they will meet ghayy' i.e., punishment. And its answer is like the answer of al-Jubba'i's interpretation: that He intends to punish them while He intends their disbelief, or He intends to punish them while He intends their faith? Whichever answer he gives, the discourse is as we mentioned. He mentioned these aspects and narrated each interpretation from its author, 'Abd al-Jabbar al-Razi, then said: 'All of this is clear.' If he means it is clear in terms of its falsehood, then it is as he intended. If he means it is clear in terms of its correctness, then he is saying a statement that necessitates shame from people and seeking forgiveness from Allah Almighty, and amazement at a man who claims leadership over the people of his sect and deep knowledge of the sciences of his companions, then is satisfied with such weak interpretations, despite their flimsiness and the obviousness of their corruption at first thought. How true is the saying: 'Your love of something blinds and deafens.' And Allah Almighty said: 'And whoever Allah intends to try (fitna), you cannot avail him anything against Allah.' It was said: 'His fitna' means punishment, and it was said: His trial through stoning and killing, and intending that without intending what necessitates it is intending injustice. And their interpretation that the word of Allah 'His fitna' means His obligation and test is wrong, because the Prophet, peace be upon him, was not distressed by that, nor did he ask that Allah not obligate His servants. And Allah Almighty said: 'Those are the ones whom Allah did not intend to purify their hearts.' And according to the Mu'tazila, He intended that. There are many verses, and they have objections against them that are corrupt, and there is no point in occupying oneself with them because anyone with the least knowledge knows the falsehood of those objections.
Source pages p. 966

Commentary
This passage contains several related arguments. First, the author extends the same dilemma from the previous discussion to another interpretation: that 'yuridu an yughwiyakum' means 'He will punish you'. The same question arises: does God intend to punish them while intending their disbelief or while intending their faith? Either answer leads to a contradiction. The author then criticizes 'Abd al-Jabbar al-Razi (a Mu'tazili) for claiming that these interpretations are 'clear', pointing out that if he means their falsehood is clear, then he is correct, but if he means their correctness is clear, then he is shameless. The author dismisses such weak exegesis. Second, the author discusses the interpretation of 'fitna' in the verse 'And whoever Allah intends to try (fitna), you cannot avail him anything against Allah.' The author rejects the Mu'tazili interpretation of 'fitna' as merely 'obligation and test', because the Prophet was not distressed by that. Instead, it refers to punishment or trial through stoning and killing, implying that intending such without the deserving cause is injustice. The author concludes that the Mu'tazila's objections to the verses are corrupt and not worth engaging with.

غيّ
فتنة
عبد الجبار الرازي

Misconception: Reinterpreting divine verses can avoid theological difficulties.
Correction: The article shows that reinterpretations introduce new contradictions and ignore context and prophetic practice.

C) It is a valid interpretation according to the Mu'tazila.
D) It is clear to those with knowledge.

Key Takeaway
The Maturidi approach defends divine justice by keeping the literal meaning of verses without forced reinterpretations.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

What does this lesson's criticism of the Mu'tazila teach you about the danger of forcing interpretations?
?
The Prophet ﷺ was not distressed by the trials of faith, nor did he ask Allah to remove obligations. Are you ever distressed when Allah commands you something difficult? Do you find yourself wishing He had not obligated you in certain matters? What does that reveal about your heart's submission to divine will?

Rational Proof of the Effectiveness of God's Will
Rational proof against Mu'tazila on divine will and refutation of dualism.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Mu'tazila position that God's will can be frustrated leads to absurd consequences and even dualism.

Core Idea
If God's will could be frustrated, creatures would be stronger than God.

This lesson presents a rational argument from Imam al-Nasafi against the Mu'tazila claim that God's will is not necessarily effective. Using simple logical reasoning, the author shows that if a disbeliever's will could override God's, it would imply the creature's will is more powerful—an impossibility for God. He then draws an analogy with a weak king and refutes the proof of mutual hindrance, warning that such thinking validates dualism.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation. Notice the argument structure: it begins with a conditional, then draws an implication, uses an analogy, and concludes with a refutation.
The passage is dense; take your time to follow the logic.
2
Identify the key premise
The argument hinges on the conditional: if God wills faith from a disbeliever, the disbeliever wills disbelief, and disbelief occurs, then God's will is frustrated by the creature's will.
This premise is used to show absurdity.
3
Consider the analogy
The author analogizes to a king whose will is not executed in his kingdom—a sign of weakness. Applying this to God is impossible.
The analogy strengthens the point that God's will must be effective.
4
Understand the refutation of dualism
The argument concludes that the Mu'tazila position invalidates the proof of mutual hindrance (al-tamānu') and leads to dualism, which is false.
This shows the stakes: denying God's effective will leads to heresy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والمعقول أنه تعالى لو شاء من الكافر الإيمان والكافر شاء من نفسه الكفر، ثم كان الكفر دون الإيمان لتعطلت مشيئة الله تعالى بمشيئة الكافر، وكانت مشيئة الكافر أنفذ من مشيئة الله تعالى وكذا مشيئة إبليس لعنه الله أنفذ في سلطان الله تعالى من مشيئة الله تعالى لكون أكثر الخلق كافرين، وكذا من أدل الدلائل على ضعف الملك وعجزه أن يوجد في ملكه ما لا يشاء، ويشاء أشياء فلا تكون، ولا يشاء أشياء فتكون على كره منه، ووصف الله تعالى بذلك محال، وهذا يرد على دلالة التمانع بالإبطال ويؤدي إلى تصحيح مذهب الثنوية.
And the rationally intelligible [argument] is that if God Almighty willed faith from the disbeliever, and the disbeliever willed from himself disbelief, and then disbelief occurred instead of faith, then God's will would be frustrated by the disbeliever's will, and the disbeliever's will would be more effective than God's will. Likewise, Iblis's will (may God curse him) would be more effective in God's dominion than God's will, because most creatures are disbelievers. Likewise, among the clearest proofs of a king's weakness and incapacity is that something he does not will exists in his kingdom, and he wills things and they do not happen, and he does not will things and they happen against his will. Describing God Almighty with that is impossible. This refutes the proof of mutual hindrance (al-tamānu') by invalidating it and leads to the validation of the dualist doctrine.
Source pages p. 967

Commentary
This passage presents a rational argument (ma'qūl) against the Mu'tazila position that God's will is not necessarily effective. The author argues by premise: if God wills faith from a disbeliever and the disbeliever wills disbelief, and disbelief occurs, then God's will is frustrated by the creature's will. This would imply the creature's will is more effective—which is impossible for God. The same applies to Iblis: if most people are disbelievers following Iblis's will, then Iblis's will would be more effective in God's dominion than God's own will, which is absurd. The author then draws an analogy: in a human king, if things happen against his will, it shows weakness; applying this to God is impossible. This argument also refutes the proof of mutual hindrance (al-tamānu') used to prove God's unity, because if God's will could be thwarted, dualism gains foothold. Thus, the argument shows that Mu'tazila position logically leads to dualism, which is false.

Key Terms
المعقول
المشيئة
الضعف
التمانع
الثنوية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: God's will can be ineffective or overridden by creatures.
Correction: God's will is always effective; if it were not, creatures would be stronger than God, which is impossible. The Mu'tazila position leads to dualism.

Checkpoint
What does the author claim would follow if God's will could be frustrated by a disbeliever's will?
A) It would prove God's mercy.
B) It would make the disbeliever's will more effective than God's, which is impossible, and would lead to dualism.
C) It would show that God chooses not to impose His will.
D) It would demonstrate the disbeliever's free will.

Key Takeaway
God's will is never frustrated; allowing otherwise would imply creature superiority and lead to dualism.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think of a time when you desperately wanted something and it didn't happen. Did you inwardly feel that your will had been 'overruled' by God? How does this lesson challenge that feeling, and what does it demand you change in your heart towards God's decree?
?
This lesson says that if God's will could be frustrated, it would be a sign of weakness—a quality absolutely impossible for Him. Is there any area of your life where you act as if your choices can genuinely oppose God's plan? In concrete terms, what would it look like to live in full submission to the effectiveness of His will?
?
The author uses the analogy of a king whose commands are ignored. Have you ever been in a position of responsibility (parent, manager, etc.) and felt powerless when those under you disobeyed? How does that human experience help you appreciate the absolute authority of God? What one change will you make today to honor that authority?

Refuting Abu Hudhayl's Interpretation of Divine Will
Author refutes Abu Hudhayl's interpretation of divine will as compulsion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author refutes Abu Hudhayl's claim that divine will means God creates faith by compulsion, using the Mu'tazilites' own principle that the agent of an action is its doer.

Core Idea
If God creates faith by force, He becomes the believer, not the human.

The Mu'tazilites held that humans are the true agents of their actions, denying that God creates human acts. Abu Hudhayl interpreted verses about divine will as God creating faith by compulsion. The author turns their own principle against them, showing the logical consequence makes God the believer.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Mu'tazilite position
Recall that Mu'tazilites believe humans create their own actions and deny God as creator of acts, otherwise God would be the doer of evil.
This is key to the refutation.
2
Read the passage and identify Abu Hudhayl's claim
Find where Abu Hudhayl defines 'will of restriction and compulsion' as God creating faith in people without their choice.
The author quotes his view directly.
3
Analyze the objection
See how the author argues that if God creates faith, He is the agent, so according to Mu'tazilite logic, He becomes the believer, not the servant. This invalidates the verses they cite.
The author uses their own principle to refute them.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
Notice that the author declares the Mu'tazilite interpretation nullifies the meaning of the Quranic verses about guidance.
The verses would only mean God guides Himself, not others.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والجواب عنه أن نقول: أي شيء تعنون بمشيئة القصر والجبر؟ فتفرقوا عند ذلك في تفسيرها، فزعم أبو الهذيل ومن تابعه أن تفسير ذلك بأن يخلق فيهم الإيمان جبراً بدون اختيارهم فيوجد فيهم الإيمان ويندفع الكفر. قيل لهم: إن من مذهبكم أن المؤمن هو فاعل الإيمان والكافر هو فاعل الكفر، ولهذا أبيتم أن يكون الله تعالى خالقاً لأفعال الخلق لأنه لو كان خالقاً لكان هو المؤمن الكافر المطيع العاصي المصلي الصائم، فعلى هذا لو خلق فيهم الإيمان لكان هو المؤمن لا العباد فلا يتصور إيمانهم ولم تنفذ مشيئة فبطل قوله: {فَلَوْ شَاءَ لَهَدَاكُمْ أَجْمَعِينَ} وقوله: {وَلَوْ شِئْنَا لَآتَيْنَا كُلَّ نَفْسٍ هُدَاهَا} إذ له قدرة جعل نفسه مؤمناً لا قدرة جعل الكافر مؤمناً، وكذا ما اندفع عنه العجز عن جعل الكافر مؤمناً بل له القدرة على جعل نفسه مؤمناً فلو شاء لأمن بنفسه وأتى نفسه هداها لا غير. ومن العجب العجيب أنه لو خلق في العبد إيماناً كسباً له باختياره وتعلقت قدرته به لم يكن العبد مؤمناً بل كان الله تعالى به مؤمناً، لأنه هو الذي أوجد الإيمان، ولو خلق فيه إيماناً وهدى بلا اختيار من جهة العبد ولا اكتساب ولا تعلق قدرته به لكان العبد مؤمناً. ولو كان الله تعالى أشرك المعتزلة في ربوبيته وفوض إليهم نصب أدلة دينه وعلق ذلك باختيارهم فأوجب على جميع الأمم الانقياد إليهم والرضا لصنيعهم والقبول لتحكمهم لكان الأولى بهم أن يستحيوا عن مثل هذا الكلام ونصب مثل هذا الدليل، فكيف ولم يوجد شيء من ذلك.
And the answer to it is that we say: What do you mean by 'the will of restriction and compulsion'? So they differed in its interpretation. Abu Hudhayl and his followers claimed that its interpretation is that He creates faith in them by compulsion without their choice, so faith comes to exist in them and disbelief is repelled. It was said to them: It is part of your doctrine that the believer is the doer of faith and the disbeliever is the doer of disbelief, and for this reason you refused that Allah Most High is the creator of the actions of creatures, because if He were the creator, He would be the believer, the disbeliever, the obedient, the disobedient, the prayer-performing, the fasting-performing. So on this, if He created faith in them, He would be the believer, not the servants, so their faith would not be conceivable, and the will would not be executed. Thus His statement is invalidated: {For if He willed, He would have guided you all} and His statement: {And if We willed, We would give every soul its guidance} because He has the power to make Himself a believer, not the power to make the disbeliever a believer. Similarly, incapacity to make the disbeliever a believer is not repelled from Him, but rather He has power to make Himself a believer; so if He willed, He would believe by Himself and give His own soul its guidance, no other. And from the strangest of wonders is that if He created in the servant faith as an acquisition for him by his choice and his power was attached to it, the servant would not be a believer, but rather Allah Most High would be a believer through it, because He is the one who brought faith into existence; and if He created in him faith and guidance without choice on the servant's part, nor acquisition, nor attachment of his power to it, the servant would be a believer. And if Allah Most High had made the Mu'tazila partners in His lordship and delegated to them the establishment of the proofs of His religion and attached that to their choice, and then obligated all nations to submit to them, be pleased with their actions, and accept their arbitrary judgments, it would be more fitting for them to be ashamed of such speech and the establishment of such a proof. But how could that be, when none of that has occurred?
Source pages p. 968

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Mu'tazilite interpretation of divine will as compulsion (mashi'ah al-qasr wa al-jabr). The author begins by asking what they mean by this term, noting that they differ in its explanation. Abu Hudhayl and his followers interpret it as God creating faith in people by force without their choice, resulting in faith and removal of disbelief. The author then objects using the Mu'tazilites' own principles: they hold that the believer is the doer of faith and the disbeliever is the doer of disbelief, and they deny that God creates human actions because that would make God the agent—making Him the believer, disbeliever, etc. The author argues that if God created faith by force, He would be the believer, not the servants, so their faith would not occur and God's will would not be fulfilled. This invalidates verses like 'If He willed, He would have guided you all' because God only has power to make Himself a believer, not to make a disbeliever a believer. The author then highlights a strange inconsistency: if God created faith in a servant as an acquisition (kasb) with the servant's choice and power, the servant would not be a believer according to their logic—God would be the believer. Yet if God created faith without any acquisition or power from the servant, the servant would be a believer. This inverts their expected outcome. Finally, the author sarcastically suggests that if the Mu'tazila were partners with God in lordship, they should be ashamed of such reasoning, but in reality they are not.

Key Terms
مشيئة القصر والجبر
أبو الهذيل
خالق أفعال الخلق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that divine will to guide means God forces faith on people, making them believers without their choice.
Correction: The author shows that if God forces faith, then according to Mu'tazilite principles, God becomes the believer, not the person, so the person is not actually guided.

Checkpoint
According to the author, why does the Mu'tazilite interpretation of divine will as compulsion invalidate the verse 'If He willed, He would have guided you all'?
A) Because God cannot guide anyone against their will.
B) Because God only has power to make Himself a believer, not to make a disbeliever a believer.
C) Because the verse is metaphorical.
D) Because the Mu'tazilites reject that God creates actions.

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazilite principle that the agent of an action is its doer is used against their own interpretation of divine will, showing that God would become the believer, not the human.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever treat your faith as something passively received, as if God forced it upon you, forgetting that you are the doer of your own belief? How can you actively choose faith today?
?
When you read 'if God willed, He would have guided you all', do you feel a sense of security or a call to action? What would it change in your life if you truly believed that your own will matters in your guidance?
?
If God were the sole agent of your faith, would you still feel accountable for your disbelief? Examine your heart: are there areas where you blame God for your shortcomings instead of taking responsibility?
